	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Central American and Caribbean Games</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Games" title="Central American Games">Central American Games</a>.</div>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">Central American and Caribbean Games (CACGs) <br /> <small><i>Juegos Centroamericanos y del Caribe</i> <span class="languageicon">(in Spanish)</span></small></caption><tbody><tr><th scope="row">First event</th><td class="note">October 30 – November 2, 1926</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Occur every</th><td>4 years</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Last event</th><td class="note">July 19 – August 3, 2018</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Purpose</th><td>Sports for Central American and Caribbean people</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Central American and Caribbean Games</b> (<b>CAC</b> or <b>CACGs</b>) are a <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport regional championship event</a>, held quadrennial (once every four years), typically in the middle (even) year between <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympics</a>. The Games are for countries in <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South American Caribbean countries</a>  of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.
</p><p>The Games are overseen by the <a href="/wiki/CACSO" title="CACSO">Central American and Caribbean Sports Organization</a> (CACSO) (the organization also goes by the acronym "ODECABE", from its full Spanish name: <i><b>O</b>rganización <b>De</b>portiva <b>C</b>entro<b>a</b>mericana y del Cari<b>be</b></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> They are designed to provide a step between sub-CACG-region Games held the first year following a Summer Olympics (e.g. Central American Games) and the Continental Championships, the <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games" title="Pan American Games">Pan American Games</a>, held the year before the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympics</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/2018_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="2018 Central American and Caribbean Games">The last games</a> were held in <a href="/wiki/Barranquilla" title="Barranquilla">Barranquilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> between 19 July to 3 August.The next games will be held in 2022, between 22 April~8 May in multiple venues in <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The CACGs are the oldest continuing regional games in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and only the Olympics have run longer. <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a> were the three countries present at the first games, which were then called the <i>Central American Games</i>. In 1935 their name was changed to <i>Central American and Caribbean Games</i> to reflect expanding participation. 
</p><p>A "Central American Games" does exist today, Juegos Centroamericanos, involving just <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central American</a> countries.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Editions">Editions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Editions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>The first two editions of the games were known as the "Central American Games" at the time, but the edition lineage continued after the inclusion of the Caribbean in 1935.
</p>
